            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The status of ambient temp. sodium ion batteries is reviewed in light of recent developments in anode, electrolyte and cathode materials.  These devices, although early in their stage of development, are promising for large-scale grid storage applications due to the abundance and very low cost of sodium-contg. precursors used to make the components.  The engineering knowledge developed recently for highly successful Li ion batteries can be leveraged to ensure rapid progress in this area, although different electrode materials and electrolytes will be required for dual intercalation systems based on sodium.  In particular, new anode materials need to be identified, since the graphite anode, commonly used in lithium systems, does not intercalate sodium to any appreciable extent.  A wider array of choices is available for cathodes, including high performance layered transition metal oxides and polyanionic compds.  Recent developments in electrodes are encouraging, but a great deal of research is necessary, particularly in new electrolytes, and the understanding of the SEI films.  The engineering modeling calcns. of Na-ion battery energy d. indicate that 210 Wh kg-1 in gravimetric energy is possible for Na-ion batteries compared to existing Li-ion technol. if a cathode capacity of 200 mAh g-1 and a 500 mAh g-1 anode can be discovered with an av. cell potential of 3.3 V.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGojsFXLPEQzILVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgk_KWCnSS9wA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XntlSnurc%253D&amp;md5=fa5d7d089d261a40896cb6b03e88bfbe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1039/c3ee40847g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Room-Temperature Stationary Sodium-Ion Batteries for Large-Scale Electric Energy Storage</span>. <i>Energy Environ. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2338</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2360</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c3ee40847g</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D6%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D2338-2360%26journal%3DEnergy%2BEnviron.%2BSci.%26author%3DH.%2BPan%26author%3DY.-S.%2BHu%26author%3DL.%2BChen%26title%3DRoom-Temperature%2BStationary%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%2Bfor%2BLarge-Scale%2BElectric%2BEnergy%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc3ee40847g&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b03279&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc3ee40847g&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Room-temperature stationary sodium-ion batteries for large-scale electric energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Huilin; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2338-2360</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries have attracted great attention particularly in large-scale elec. energy storage applications for renewable energy and smart grid because of the huge abundant sodium resources and low cost.  In this article, a variety of electrode materials including cathodes and anodes as well as electrolytes for room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries are briefly reviewed.  We compare the difference in storage behavior between Na and Li in their analogous electrodes and summarize the sodium storage mechanisms in the available electrode materials.  This review also includes some new results from our group and our thoughts on developing new materials.  Some perspectives and directions on designing better materials for practical applications are pointed out based on knowledge from the literature and our experience.  Through this extensive literature review, the search for suitable electrode and electrolyte materials for stationary sodium-ion batteries is still challenging.  However, after intensive research efforts, we believe that low-cost, long-life and room-temp. sodium-ion batteries would be promising for applications in large-scale energy storage system in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpqNKJTie6WmbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgk_KWCnSS9wA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtFOisrzJ&amp;md5=2e02460553edc21e1ea8b73982ed63bb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1016/j.cossms.2012.04.002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ellis, B.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Owing to almost unmatched volumetric energy d., Li-ion batteries have dominated the portable electronics industry and solid state electrochem. literature for the past 20 years.  Not only will that continue, but they are also now powering plug-in hybrid elec. vehicles and elec. vehicles.  In light of possible concerns over rising lithium costs in the future, Na and Na-ion batteries have re-emerged as candidates for medium and large-scale stationary energy storage, esp. as a result of heightened interest in renewable energy sources that provide intermittent power which needs to be load-levelled.  The sodium-ion battery field presents many solid state materials design challenges, and rising to that call in the past couple of years, several reports of new sodium-ion technologies and electrode materials have surfaced.  These range from high-temp. air electrodes to new layered oxides, polyanion-based materials, carbons and other insertion materials for sodium-ion batteries, many of which hold promise for future sodium-based energy storage applications.  In this article, the challenges of current high-temp. sodium technologies including Na-S and Na-NiCl2 and new molten sodium technol., Na-O2 are summarized.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The room temp. Na-ion secondary battery has been under focus lately due to its feasibility to compete against the already well-established Li-ion secondary battery.  Although there are many obstacles to overcome before the Na-ion battery becomes com. available, recent research discoveries corroborate that some of the cathode materials for the Na-ion battery have indeed indisputable advantages over its Li-ion counterparts.  In this publication, a comprehensive review of layered oxides (NaTMO2, TM = Ti, V, Cr, Mn, Fe, Co, Ni, and a mixt. of 2 or 3 elements) as a viable Na-ion battery cathode is presented.  Single TM systems are well characterized not only for their electrochem. performance but also for their structural transitions during the cycle.  Binary TM systems are investigated in order to address issues regarding low reversible capacity, capacity retention, operating voltage, and structural stability.  As a consequence, some materials already have reached an energy d. of 520 mW h g-1, which is comparable to that of LiFePO4.  Furthermore, some ternary TM systems retained more than 72% of their capacity along with over 99.7% Coulombic efficiency for 275 cycles.  The goal of this review is to present the development of Na layered oxide materials in the past as well as the state of the art today in order to emphasize the compatibility and durability of layered oxides as powerful candidates for Na-ion battery cathode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpwo96Ash7WNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgk_KWCnSS9wA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitVCrsLjE&amp;md5=d938be66a2a0948e3d2f589b803dbf76</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b04557"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bucher, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hartung, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Franklin, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have become a subject of increasing interest and are considered as an alternative to the ubiquitous lithium-ion battery.  To compare the effect of two improvement strategies for metal oxide cathodes, specifically Co-doping and morphol. optimization, four representatives of the prominent material class of layered NaxMO2 (M = transition metal) have been studied: hexagonal flakes and hollow spheres of P2-NaxMnO2 and P2-NaxCo0.1Mn0.9O2.  The better electrochem. performance of the spheres over the flakes and of the Co-doped over the undoped materials are explained on the basis of structural features revealed by operando synchrotron X-ray diffraction.  The higher cycling stability of the material doped with ∼10% Co is attributed to three effects: (i) the suppression of a Jahn-Teller-induced structural transition from the initial hexagonal to an orthorhombic phase that is obsd. in NaxMnO2, (ii) suppression of ordering processes of Na+; and (iii) enhanced Na+ kinetics as revealed by galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique measurements and in situ electrochem. impedance measurements.  Increased capacity and cycling stability of spheres over flakes may be related to smaller changes of the unit cell vol. of spheres and thus to reduced structural stress.         </div><div class="casAbstract">There is a great interest in developing efficient electrode materials for Na-ion batteries, which are currently being projected as a promising alternative to Li-ion batteries. The as-synthesized layered Na0.5Ni0.25Mn0.75O2 material exhibits a layered P2-type structure, and shows excellent electrochem. properties when studied as a cathode for Na-ion batteries, with a specific discharge capacity of 210 mAh g-1 and a good capacity retention of 80% at 50th cycle in the voltage range from 1.5 to 4.4 V at 0.1 C.  The layered Na0.5Ni0.25Mn0.75O2 material also exhibits good cycling stability with remarkably smooth and flat charge-discharge profiles at a high voltage of 4.1 V vs. Na.  The overall electrochem. performance of layered Na0.5Ni0.25Mn0.75O2 is quite promising, and hence the present study will greatly contribute to the on-going search for advanced and efficient electrodes for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo6r0CFmAM2MLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liMoqIcIygG6Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XntVGitrY%253D&amp;md5=93bebc093ff70c4a2ca8872f36d4f54f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1039/c5ra06275f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile Synthesis of P2-Type Na<sub>0.4</sub>Mn<sub>0.54</sub>Co<sub>0.46</sub>O<sub>2</sub> as a High Capacity Cathode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>RSC Adv.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">51454</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">51460</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile synthesis of P2-type Na0.4Mn0.54Co0.46O2 as a high capacity cathode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Xijun; Ji, Shaomin; Gao, Ruibo; Liu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries have received great attention because of the abundant sodium resources and low cost.  As a typical kind of cathode material for Na-ion batteries, sodium manganese oxides have shown great potential in cathode application due to their high specific capacity and good rate capability.  Herein, we successfully synthesized P2-type Na0.4Mn0.54Co0.46O2 nanosheets via a two-step annealing route.  The morphol. and structural information of the Na0.4Mn0.54Co0.46O2 products were characterized by X-ray diffraction (XRD), transmission electron microscopy (TEM) and high resoln. transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM) technologies. As the cathode for Na-ion batteries, the layered Na0.4Mn0.54Co0.46O2 nanosheets showed a high second charge capacity of 194 mA h g-1 and delivered a specific capacity of 125 mA h g-1 at a current of 20 mA g-1 after 60 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpxH05VnYJXcbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liMoqIcIygG6Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXpsVyru7w%253D&amp;md5=43f4416f96865f59b7d011acfc86d59f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1039/c4ta06467d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent developments in electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Luyuan Paul; Yu, Linghui; Wang, Xin; Srinivasan, Madhavi; Xu, Zhichuan J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The rapid consumption of nonrenewable resources resulted in an ever-increasing problem of CO2 emissions that has motivated people for studying the harvesting of energy from renewable alternatives (e.g. solar and wind).  Efficient electrochem. energy storage devices play a crucial role in storing harvested energies in the daily lives.  For example, rechargeable batteries can store energy generated by solar cells during the daytime and release it during night-time.  In particular, Li-ion batteries (LIBs) have received considerable attention ever since their early commercialization in 1990s.  However, with initiatives by several governments to build large-scale energy grids to store energy for cities, problems such as the high cost and limited availability of Li starts to become major issues.  Na, which also belongs to Group 1 of the periodic table, has comparable electrochem. properties to Li, and more importantly it is considerably more accessible than Li.  Nonetheless, research into Na-ion batteries (NIBs) is currently still in its infancy compared to LIBs, although great leaps and bounds have been made recently in terms of research and development into this technol.  Here in this review, the authors summarize the recent advancements made, also covering the prospective materials for both the battery cathode and anode.  Addnl., opinions on possible solns. through correlating trends in recent papers will be suggested.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqaYAOgglkaCrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgbMRxfLCfsXg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXjs1yhsbo%253D&amp;md5=95489f575e9ded7e312db8576036b208</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.04.067"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, H.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, C.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.-H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium Insertion Cathode Material Na<sub>0.67</sub>[Ni<sub>0.4</sub>Co<sub>0.2</sub>Mn<sub>0.4</sub>]O<sub>2</sub> with Excellent Electrochemical Properties</span>. <i>Electrochim.         </div><div class="casAbstract">P2-type Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 plates with homogeneous compn. and regular morphol. were prepd. by spray pyrolysis.  The rhombohedral P3-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 microspheres formed by 1-pot spray pyrolysis transform into hexagonal P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 plates after post-treatment at 800-1000°.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rechargeable Na/Na0.44MnO2 cells with ionic liquid electrolytes containing various sodium solutes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Chueh-Han; Yeh, Yu-Wen; Wongittharom, Nithinai; Wang, Yi-Chen; Tseng, Chung-Jen; Lee, Sheng-Wei; Chang, Wen-Sheng; Chang, Jeng-Kuei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Orthorhombic Na0.44MnO2 with wide structural tunnels for sodium-ion transport is synthesized. The battery with NaClO4-incorporated ionic liq. electrolyte exhibits superior charge-discharge performance due to it having the lowest solid-electrolyte-interface resistance and charge transfer resistance at both the Na and Na0.44MnO2 electrodes.  The ionic liq. electrolyte shows high thermal stability and is suitable for use at an elevated temp.  At 75°, the measured capacity of Na0.44MnO2 in the ionic liq. electrolyte with NaClO4 is as high as 115 mA-h/g (at 0.05C), which is close to the theor. value (121 mA-h/g).  Moreover, 85% of this capacity can be retained when the charge-discharge rate is increased to 1C.  These properties are superior to those of a conventional org. electrolyte.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqBEXxRDIPh2rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgbMRxfLCfsXg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvVemtL3J&amp;md5=b0918ab7486ad24f4b59d1baf90ea094</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1039/b108830k"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Caballero, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hernán, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Morales, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sánchez, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Santos Peña, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Aranda, M.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis and characterization of high-temperature hexagonal P2-Na0.6MnO2 and its electrochemical behaviour as cathode in sodium cells</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Caballero, A.; Hernan, L.; Morales, J.; Sanchez, L.; Santos Pena, J.; Aranda, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A layered sodium manganese oxide, Na0.6MnO2, stable at temps. &gt;800°, was synthesized by using a sol-gel method that employs Mn(acac)3 (ac = acetylacetonate), Na2CO3, and propionic acid to form the resin framework.  This layered bronze possesses a hexagonal, P2-type structure, in which the distortion assocd. with Mn3+ is hardly noticeable.  It reacts slowly, though reversibly, with atm. moisture, which causes the interlayer spacing in the structure to increase by ∼2.5 Å, by intercalation of water mols. into the interlayer gap occupied by Na+ ions.  The anhyd. material was tested as a cathode in sodium cells.  Although the electrochem. intercalation of Na+ occurs in two steps, the host retains its main structural features, with a slight tendency in the interlayer spacing to contract as the sodium content increases.  The similarity between the discharge and charge profiles of the first cycles reveals a quasi-reversible nature of the intercalation process and that the cell can deliver a const. sp. capacity of ∼140 A-h/kg at 0.1 mA/cm2 when cycled in a voltage region of 3.8-2.0 V.  However, the continuous strains and distortions resulting from the insertion and extn. of Na+ ions cause the host structure to gradually collapse and yield an amorphous material after the first eight cycles.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Layered NaxMnO2+z in Sodium Ion Batteries - Influence of Morphology on Cycle Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bucher, Nicolas; Hartung, Steffen; Nagasubramanian, Arun; Cheah, Yan Ling; Hoster, Harry E.; Madhavi, Srinivasan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to its potential cost advantage, sodium ion batteries could become a com. alternative to lithium ion batteries.  One promising cathode material for this type of battery is layered sodium manganese oxide.  In this investigation the effect of morphol. on cycle performance for the layered NaxMnO2+z is reported.  Hollow spheres of NaxMnO2+z with a diam. of ∼5 μm were compared to flake-like NaxMnO2+z.  It was found that the electrochem. behavior of both materials as measured by cyclic voltammetry is comparable.  However, the cycle stability of the spheres is significantly higher, with 94 mA h g-1 discharge capacity after 100 cycles, as opposed to 73 mA h g-1 for the flakes (50 mA g-1).  The better stability can potentially be attributed to better accommodation of vol. changes of the material due to its spherical morphol., better contact with the added conductive carbon, and higher electrode/electrolyte interface owing to better wetting of the active material with the electrolyte.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpawRFnxN2xdrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljtqBA0E_c5rQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-performance symmetric sodium-ion batteries using a new, bipolar O3-type material, Na0.8Ni0.4Ti0.6O2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Shaohua; Yu, Haijun; Liu, Pan; Ren, Yang; Zhang, Tao; Chen, Mingwei; Ishida, Masayoshi; Zhou, Haoshen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Based on low-cost and rich resources, sodium-ion batteries have been regarded as a promising candidate for next-generation energy storage batteries in the large-scale energy applications of renewable energy and smart grids. In this work, a stable sym. sodium-ion battery based on the bipolar, active O3-type material, Na0.8Ni0.4Ti0.6O2, is developed.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The 1st review of the various electrolytes currently used and developed for Na-ion batteries (SIBs), both in terms of materials and concepts, is presented.  In contrast to the Li-ion battery (LIB), which is a mature technol. for which a more or less unanimously accepted std. electrolyte exists: 1 M LiPF6 in EC/DMC, the electrolyte of choice for SIBs has not yet fully conformed to a std.  This is true for both materials: salts, solvents, or additives, and concept, using the main track of org. solvents or aiming for other concepts.  SIB research currently prospers, benefitting from using know-how gained from 30 years of LIB R and D.  Here the currently employed electrolytes are emphasized and their effects on practical SIB performance are outlined, scrutinizing the rationale for specific choices made, salts, solvents, additives, concns., etc. for each specific cell set-up and usage conditions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpb_d9E3Qe0wLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljtqBA0E_c5rQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhslOjtLfI&amp;md5=b99d9ac3e00e101e25ffc33ee1bef953</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201301563"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ahn, H.-j.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Single Crystalline Na<sub>0.7</sub>mno<sub>2</sub> Nanoplates as Cathode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries with Enhanced Performance</span>. <i>Chem.—Eur.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Single cryst. rhombus-shaped Na0.7MnO2 nanoplates have been synthesized by a hydrothermal method.  TEM and HRTEM analyses revealed that the Na0.7MnO2 single crystals predominantly exposed their (100) crystal plane, which is active for Na+-ion insertion and extn.  When applied as cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries, Na0.7MnO2 nanoplates exhibited a high reversible capacity of 163 mA h g-1, a satisfactory cyclability, and a high rate performance.  The enhanced electrochem. performance could be ascribed to the predominantly exposed active (100) facet, which could facilitate fast Na+-ion insertion/extn. during the discharge and charge process.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoX3VNBpVhls7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljtqBA0E_c5rQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtFShtrjK&amp;md5=1e83832ef6024defad3041c72abe632d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2006.03.016"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Galiński, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lewandowski, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Stępniak, I.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ionic Liquids as Electrolytes</span>. <i>Electrochim.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ionic liquids as electrolytes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Galinski, Maciej; Lewandowski, Andrzej; Stepniak, Izabela</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2006</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">51</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">26</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Salts having a low m.p. are liq. at room temp., or even below, and form a new class of liqs. usually called room temp. ionic liqs. (RTIL).  Information about RTILs can be found in the literature with such key words as: room temp. molten salt, low-temp. molten salt, ambient-temp. molten salt, liq. org. salt or simply ionic liq.  Their physicochem. properties are the same as high temp. ionic liqs., but the practical aspects of their maintenance or handling are different enough to merit a distinction.  The class of ionic liqs., based on tetraalkylammonium cation and chloroaluminate anion, was extensively studied since late 1970s of the XX century, following the works of Osteryoung.  Systematic research on the application of chloroaluminate ionic liqs. as solvents was performed in 1980s.  However, ionic liqs. based on Al halides are moisture sensitive.  During the last decade an increasing no. of new ionic liqs. were prepd. and used as solvents.  The general aim of this paper was to review the phys. and chem. properties of RTILs from the point of view of their possible application as electrolytes in electrochem. processes and devices.  The following points are discussed: melting and freezing, cond., viscosity, temp. dependence of cond., transport and transference nos., electrochem. stability, possible application in Al electroplating, Li batteries and in electrochem. capacitors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo28DRQSuLWGLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lie8AXThfh3gg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD28XotVaqtr8%253D&amp;md5=09823d6515f7af16484295909b7b10e9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1002/cphc.201402175"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tan, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, Y.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent Progress in Research on High-Voltage Electrolytes for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tan, Shi; Ji, Ya J.; Zhang, Zhong R.; Yang, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemPhysChem</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review of recent progress in the development of several promising high-voltage (.ltorsim.5 V) electrolyte systems, as well as their "recipes" (for synthesis), electrochem. performance, electrode compatibility, and characterization methods.  These new electrolyte systems include high-voltage film-forming additives and new solvents, such as sulfones, ionic liqs., nitriles, and fluorinated carbonates.  It appears to be very difficult to find a good high-voltage (∼5 V) electrolyte with a single-component solvent at the present stage.  Other topics discussed include: (1) stabilizing the cathode-electrolyte interface with additives and surface coating, (2) new types of solvents for high-voltage electrolytes, (3) sulfone-based solvents, (4) ionic liq.-based systems, (5) nitrile co-solvents, and (6) derivs. of carbonate-based systems.  Using mixed fluorinated-carbonate solvents and additives are two realistic solns. for practical applications in the near term, while sulfones, nitriles, ionic liqs. and solid-state electrolyte/polymer electrolytes are promising candidates for the next generation of high-voltage electrolyte systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr2q6nFGTWCRrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lie8AXThfh3gg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtFGqsL7O&amp;md5=78ba3560dc049a180938145aff5f9e6c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201703491"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Basile, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hilder, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Makhlooghiazad, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pozo-Gonzalo, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">MacFarlane, D.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ionic Liquid Electrolytes with Various Sodium Solutes for Rechargeable Na/NaFePO4 Batteries Operated at Elevated Temperatures</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wongittharom, Nithinai; Wang, Chueh-Han; Wang, Yi-Chen; Yang, Cheng-Hsien; Chang, Jeng-Kuei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">NaFePO4 with an olivine structure is synthesized via chem. delithiation of LiFePO4 followed by electrochem. sodiation of FePO4.  Butylmethylpyrrolidinium-bis(trifluoromethanesulfonyl)imide (BMP-TFSI) ionic liq. (IL) with various sodium solutes, namely NaBF4, NaClO4, NaPF6, and NaN(CN)2, is used as an electrolyte for rechargeable Na/NaFePO4 cells. (above 50 °C), the IL electrolyte is more suitable than a conventional org. electrolyte for the sodium cell.  At 75 °C, the measured capacity of NaFePO4 in a NaBF4-incorporated IL electrolyte is as high as 152 mAh g-1 (at 0.05 C), which is near the theor. value (154 mAh g-1). This IL electrolyte shows high thermal stability (&gt; 400°) and non-flammability, and is thus ideal for high-safety applications.  The effects of NaTFSI concn. (0.1-1.0 M) on cell performance at 25 and 50° are studied. This ratio (reflecting the rate capability) is higher than that found in a traditional org. electrolyte.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-ion batteries, recent advances and present challenges to become low cost energy storage systems</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Palomares, Veronica; Serras, Paula; Villaluenga, Irune; Hueso, Karina B.; Carretero-Gonzalez, Javier; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRYtxfVVW_sLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liZmDiGcUpfYg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XivFWnu7s%253D&amp;md5=72869139086b8ee9adec746418ff84b1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1149/2.0091513jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Iermakova, D.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">On the Comparative Stability of Li and Na Metal Anode Interfaces in Conventional Alkyl Carbonate Electrolytes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Iermakova, D. I.; Dugas, R.; Palacin, M. R.; Ponrouch, A.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">162</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">13</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A comparative study of the electrode/electrolyte interface was carried out for lithium and sodium metal anodes in electrolytes consisting in 1 M LiPF6 in EC0.5:DMC0.5 (LP30) and 1 M NaPF6 in both EC0.5:DMC0.5 and EC0.45PC0.45DMC0.1.  Sym. Li/Li cells exhibited low polarization and smooth charge discharge curves with current densities of 0.1 and 1 mA/cm2.  In contrast, large overpotentials were obsd. even at 0.1 mA/cm2 for Na/Na cells.  Such differences cannot be related to ionic cond. of the electrolytes but are rather due to an enhanced interfacial resistance (Rct + RSEI) as deduced from impedance measurements.  The compn. of the SEI layer was investigated by FTIR and found to be stable for Li electrodes but to evolve upon cycling for Na electrodes which is also in agreement with differences in surface morphol. detected by SEM.  A lower stability (partial soly.) of the SEI would also enable to understand the differences in the impedance of identical hard carbon (HC) electrodes in cells with either Li or Na counterelectrodes.  These results cast some concerns on the reliability of the so termed half cell characterization and call for caution when interpreting the results of potential electrode materials for sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrfmKjOY-ohXrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liZmDiGcUpfYg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1Gksr3E&amp;md5=6427884e168c7d538e1fdcda1601c226</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1149/2.0411707jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tchitchekova, D.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">On the Reliability of Half-Cell Tests for Monovalent (Li+, Na+) and Divalent (Mg2+, Ca2+) Cation Based Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tchitchekova, D. S.; Monti, D.; Johansson, P.; Barde, F.; Randon-Vitanova, A.; Palacein, M. R.; Ponrouch, A.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">164</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">A1384-A1392</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JESOAN</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A comprehensive study is reported entailing a comparison of Li, Na, K, Mg, and Ca based electrolytes and an investigation of the reliability of electrochem. tests using half-cells.  Ionic cond., viscosity, and Raman spectroscopy results point to the cation-solvent interaction to follow the polarizing power of the cations, i.e. Mg2+ &gt; Ca2+&gt; Li+ &gt; Na+ &gt; K+ and to divalent cation based electrolytes having stronger tendency to form ion pairs - lowering the cation accessibility and mobility.  Both increased temp. and the use of anions with delocalized neg. charge, such as TFSI, are effective in mitigating this issue.  Another factor impeding the divalent cations mobility is the larger solvation shells, as compared to those of monovalent cations, that in conjunction with stronger solvent - cation interactions contribute to slower charge transfer and ultimately a large impedance of Mg and Ca electrodes.  An important consequence is the non-reliability of the pseudo-ref. electrodes as these present both significant potential shifts as well as unstable behaviors.  Finally, exptl. protocols in order to achieve consistent results when using half-cell set-ups are proposed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoYVByTpUG3lrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgTH3jjM7aZeA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhtVCitL%252FM&amp;md5=b6e1096a51533a1e8108f4561f8cc48c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1149/2.0981610jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dugas, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ponrouch, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gachot, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">David, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Palacin, M.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na Reactivity toward Carbonate-Based Electrolytes: The Effect of FEC as Additive</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dugas, R.; Ponrouch, A.; Gachot, G.; David, R.; Palacin, M. R.; Tarascon, J. M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">163</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have regained attention because they offer sustainability advantages over the Li-ion technol., hence their interest for massive electrochem. storage.  Although the Na-ion electrochem. is analogous to that of the Li-ion concept, there are a few notable differences such as the stability of carbonated-based electrolytes toward the Li or Na metal anodes.  Herein we report on the pos. effect of FEC as electrolyte additive on the efficiency of Na-half cells which unfortunately comes with a side effect involving the sudden onset of polarization during discharge at unpredictable capacity values.  We show that these anomalies, assocd. to an inefficient plating-stripping at the sodium metal anode, do not appear in full Na-ion cells.  Therefore, FEC-based electrolytes are not the panacea and alternative additives must be sought to enable building of reliable half cells with metal anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGogrGGmLDUqu7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgTH3jjM7aZeA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsV2ks7vO&amp;md5=9a000eab51d3c08f3c70dc689fead17a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2013.02.109"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Buchholz, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chagas, L.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report the electrochem. performance of Na0.45Ni0.22Co0.11Mn0.66O2 as cathode material for lithium and sodium batteries.  The material is able to reversibly accommodate both cation species but shows a much better electrochem. performance towards Na-ion intercalation.  Upon galvanostatic cycling for 100 cycles a much higher capacity retention (82% vs. Na, 61% vs. Li) and higher coulombic efficiency (99.5% vs. Na, 98.5% vs. Li) are shown by the sodium-based system.  The worse electrochem. performance of the lithium-based system can be explained by the much higher irreversibility of the Mn3+/Mn4+ redox process.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrz2VI7xXDNkrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgTH3jjM7aZeA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXltVers70%253D&amp;md5=65b6c37de11e2a517c95e66f93519e35</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.06.003"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Monti, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ponrouch, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Palacín, M.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Towards safer sodium-ion batteries via organic solvent/ionic liquid based hybrid electrolytes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Monti, Damien; Ponrouch, Alexandre; Palacin, M. Rosa; Johansson, Patrik</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">324</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hybrid electrolytes aimed at application in sodium-ion batteries (SIB) consisting of an org. solvent mixt. (EC:PC) and different ionic liqs. (ILs); EMImTFSI, BMImTFSI, and Pyr13TFSI, and with the NaTFSI salt providing the Na+ charge carriers have here been extensively studied.  The physico-chem. and electrochem. characterization includes ionic cond., viscosity, d., cation coordination and solvation, various safety measures, and electrochem. stability window (ESW).  Hybrid electrolytes with 10-50% of IL content were found to have ionic conductivities on par with comparable org. solvent based electrolytes, but with highly enhanced safety properties.  A systematic Raman spectroscopy study of the cation coordination and solvation before and after electrolyte safety tests by ignition suggest that IL cations and TFSI remain stable when ignited while org. solvents are consumed.  Finally, the solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) formed when using hybrid electrolytes has both better mech. and electrochem. stability than the SEI derived from pure IL based electrolytes.  For a half-cell with a hard carbon (HC) electrode and a hybrid electrolyte with a compn. of 0.8 m NaTFSI in EC0.45:PC0.45:Pyr13TFSI0.10 encouraging results were obtained for IL based electrolytes - ca. 182 mAhg-1 at C/10 over 40 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoWLV5XXOvRMrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgTH3jjM7aZeA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XpsVGku70%253D&amp;md5=136b0f8f71be340adaf89dacc6942321</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.08.025"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Plylahan, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kerner, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lim, D.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Matic, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Johansson, P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ionic Liquid and Hybrid Ionic Liquid/Organic Electrolytes for High Temperature Lithium-Ion Battery Application</span>. <i>Electrochim.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ionic liquid and hybrid ionic liquid/organic electrolytes for high temperature lithium-ion battery application</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Plylahan, Nareerat; Kerner, Manfred; Lim, Du-Hyun; Matic, Aleksandar; Johansson, Patrik</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">216</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ionic liq. (IL) and hybrid IL/org. electrolytes with pyrrolidinium cation based ILs were studied for application in high temp. Li-ion batteries (HT-LIBs).  The IL based electrolytes show high thermal stabilities, up to 340°, ionic conductivities of &gt;5 × 10-3 S cm-1 at 80°, and broad electrochem. stability windows: 0-5 V vs. Li+/Li°.  The performance of LiFePO4 based half-cells at 80° is promising, delivering ∼160 mAh g-1 at 1 C, with a rate capability up to 4 C and ∼98% coulombic efficiency.  The creation of hybrid IL/org. electrolytes by adding different org. cyclic carbonate solvents reduces viscosity of the electrolytes by 28% at 80°, thereby improving the ion transport, and further improves the electrochem. performance; higher stability, better rate capability, and ≥99% coulombic efficiency.  Overall, the electrolytes proposed have a potential to be applied in HT-LIBs, a concept with large advantages at the vehicle system level.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoFrvzjWfzkr7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgTH3jjM7aZeA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsVyhsbjE&amp;md5=f4eb6aec36c909564973e50e79be7397</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1039/c7ta04599a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chanthad, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oh, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ayhan, I.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Organic-inorganic hybrid electrolytes from ionic liquid-functionalized octasilsesquioxane for lithium metal batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Guang; Chanthad, Chalathorn; Oh, Hyukkeun; Ayhan, Ismail Alperen; Wang, Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The use of highly conductive solid-state electrolytes to replace conventional liq. org. electrolytes enables radical improvements in the reliability, safety, and performance of lithium batteries.  Here, the synthesis and characterization are reported of a new class of nonflammable solid electrolytes based on the grafting of ionic liqs. onto octa-silsesquioxane.  The electrolyte exhibits outstanding room-temp. ionic cond. (∼4.8 × 10-4 S cm-1), excellent electrochem. stability (up to 5 V relative to Li+/Li) and high thermal stability.  All-solid-state Li metal batteries using the prepd. electrolyte membrane are successfully cycled with high coulombic efficiencies at ambient temp.  The good cycling stability of the electrolyte against lithium has been demonstrated.  This work provides a new platform for the development of solid polymer electrolytes for application in room-temp. lithium batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoTdZANov7JXbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liM1h4feKX33w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhsVant7rF&amp;md5=79c04a82498537e117cdf9e52ffbf471</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2015.01.095"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Arun, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Aravindan, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ling, W.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Importance of nanostructure for reversible Li-insertion into octahedral sites of LiNi0.5Mn1.5O4 and its application towards aqueous Li-ion chemistry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Arun, Nagasubramanian; Aravindan, Vanchiappan; Ling, Wong Chui; Madhavi, Srinivasan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We demonstrate the significance of nanostructuring on the reversible Li-insertion into octahedral sites of the nickel substituted spinel LiNi0.5Mn1.5O4.  One-dimensional nanofibers (50-250 nm diam.) of the LiNi0.5Mn1.5O4 were prepd. by a single spinneret electrospinning and their performance was compared with powders synthesized via a conventional solid state approach.  Li-diffusion coeff. of electrospun fibers was an order of magnitude higher (5.8 × 10-11 cm2/s) than that of conventional powders (1.22 × 10-12 cm2/s).  Galvanostatic studies revealed a much improved capacity and rate performance for electrospun fibers.  The fibers delivered a reversible capacity of ∼87 mA-h/g after 150 cycles at 1C rate compared to negligible capacity for solid-state prepd. material.  Finally, the performance of this nanostructured spinel phase as an anode in aq. rechargeable Li-ion system was demonstrated to require a strongly alk. electrolyte.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGogXU_r6VIrmrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liM1h4feKX33w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtVGhtbo%253D&amp;md5=5c002ed6c3d86334c42782b77c6c5bcf</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1149/1.3298903"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Plashnitsa, L.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Performance of NASICON symmetric cell with ionic liquid electrolyte</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Plashnitsa, Larisa S.; Kobayashi, Eiji; Noguchi, Yoshinori; Okada, Shigeto; Yamaki, Jin-ichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">To improve the thermal stability of lithium- and sodium-ion batteries, the room-temp. molten salts LiBF4/1-ethyl-3-Me imidazolium tetrafluoroborate (EMIBF4) and NaBF4/EMIBF4 were used as ionic liq. (IL) electrolytes instead of flammable carbonate-type org. electrolyte solvents.  To avoid cathodic decompn. of the IL electrolytes, a sym. cell configuration with Na Superionic CONductor (NASICON)-type A3V2(PO4)3 (where A is Li or Na) as both cathode and anode was tried in a coin-type cell (type 2320). The substitution of the org. electrolytes by the appropriate IL electrolytes in both cases resulted in the redn. in the first discharge capacities.  However, the IL-based cells revealed better cyclability and a more stable behavior at elevated temps.  The obtained electrochem. behavior of the sym. cells was confirmed by the complex impedance measurements at 25 and 80°C.  In addn., the thermal stability of LVP and NVP with the IL electrolytes was also examd.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp0NIvEGagi0rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liM1h4feKX33w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXjt1amu7c%253D&amp;md5=50b40290ba179a0d85d8c7732d604748</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1021/jp3019815"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nguyen, C.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Understanding the Interfacial Processes at Silicon-Copper Electrodes in Ionic Liquid Battery Electrolyte</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nguyen, Cao Cuong; Woo, Sang-Wook; Song, Seung-Wan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The interfacial processes at an amorphous Si-Cu (Si-Cu) electrode in the ionic liq. electrolyte of 1 M Li bis(trifluoromethanesulfonyl)imide/1-methyl-1-propylpyrrolidinium bis(trifluoromethylsulfonyl)imide (LiTFSI/Py1,3TFSI) during initial charge-discharge cycle are studied by characterizing the solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) compn. at different states of charge using ex situ attenuated total reflection FTIR spectroscopy combined with XPS.  The analyses data reveal that in the early stage of charge (1.5 V vs. Li/Li+), alkylated Si and ester-contg. species 1st form by the reductive decompn. of Py1,3 ion, and LiF salt and Si-F bond-contg. compd. 1st form by the decompn. of TFSI anion, resp.  TFSI decompn. is obsd. to begin with the C-F cleavage, which was proposed as the cleavage of N-S bond in the previous reports.  Charging to lower voltage thickens the SEI layer, but lithiation of Si results in damage or destabilization of the existing SEI probably due to changes in structural vol. together with particle morphol.  The SEI layer is however reversibly rebuilt in delithiation.  The data provide a basic understanding of the SEI formation mechanism on the Si-based anodes in ionic liq. electrolyte for less flammable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrd9CZjUdjw4bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liM1h4feKX33w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XoslGjsb4%253D&amp;md5=eafd14bab83bbd5e946d63eb0af6bcc5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2008.05.036"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sugimoto, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kikuta, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ishiko, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kono, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ishikawa, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ionic Liquid Electrolytes Compatible with Graphitized Carbon Negative without Additive and Their Effects on Interfacial Properties</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ionic liquid electrolytes compatible with graphitized carbon negative without additive and their effects on interfacial properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sugimoto, Toshinori; Kikuta, Manabu; Ishiko, Eriko; Kono, Michiyuki; Ishikawa, Masashi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Introduction of bis(fluorosulfonyl)imide (FSI) as an anion to an ambient-temp. ionic liq. electrolyte based on 1-ethyl-3-methylimidazolium (EMI) as well as lithium (Li) cations can provide a reversible Li intercalation into a graphitized electrode, while such intercalation is completely irreversible without FSI. Ac impedance spectroscopy revealed that the resistance of the electrode charged with FSI was much lower even than that charged in a solvent electrolyte system contg. ethylene carbonate (EC) and di-Me carbonate (DMC).                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Influence of Polar Organic Solvents in an Ionic Liquid Containing Lithium Bis(fluorosulfonyl)amide: Effect on the Cation-Anion Interaction, Lithium Ion Battery Performance, and Solid Electrolyte Interphase</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lahiri, Abhishek; Li, Guozhu; Olschewski, Mark; Endres, Frank</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ionic liq.-org. solvent mixts. have recently been investigated as potential battery electrolytes.  However, contradictory results with these mixts. have been shown for battery performance.  In this manuscript, we studied the influence of the addn. of polar org. solvents into the ionic liq. electrolyte 1 M lithium bis(fluorosulfonyl)amide (LiFSI)-1-butyl-1-methylpyrrolidinium bis(fluorosulfonyl)amide ([Py1,4]FSI) and tested it for lithium ion battery applications.  From IR and Raman spectroscopy, clear changes in the lithium solvation and cation-anion interactions in the ionic liq. were obsd. on addn. of org. solvents.  From the lithiation/delithiation studies on electrodeposited Ge, the storage capacity for the ionic liq.-highly polar org. solvent (acetonitrile) mixt. was found to be the highest at low C-rates (0.425 C) compared to using an ionic liq. alone and ionic liq.-less polar solvent (di-Me carbonate) mixts.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A comprehensive study on the cell chemistry of the sodium superoxide (NaO2) battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hartmann, Pascal; Bender, Conrad L.; Sann, Joachim; Duerr, Anna Katharina; Jansen, Martin; Janek, Juergen; Adelhelm, Philipp</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Chemistry Chemical Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This work reports on the cell chem. of a room temp. sodium-oxygen battery using an electrolyte of diethylene glycol di-Me ether (diglyme) and sodium trifluoromethanesulfonate (NaSO3CF3, sodium triflate).  Different from lithium-oxygen cells, where lithium peroxide is found as the discharge product, sodium superoxide (NaO2) is formed in the present cell, with overpotentials as low as 100 mV during charging.  Several anal. methods are used to follow the cell reaction during discharge and charge.  Changes in structure and morphol. are studied by SEM and XRD.  It is found that NaO2 grows as cubic particles with feed sizes in the range of 10-50 μm; upon recharge the particles consecutively decomp.  Pressure monitoring during galvanostatic cycling shows that the coulombic efficiency (e-/O2) for discharge and charge is approx. 1.0, the expected value for NaO2 formation.  Also optical spectroscopy is identified as a convenient and useful tool to follow the discharge-charge process.  The max. discharge capacity is found to be limited by oxygen transport within the electrolyte soaked carbon fiber cathode and pore blocking near the oxygen interface is obsd.  Finally electrolyte decompn. and sodium dendrite growth are identified as possible reasons for the limited capacity retention of the cell.  The occurrence of undesired side reactions is analyzed by DEMS measurements during cycling as well as by post mortem XPS investigations.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGopL5ra_RP_GLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljzdXv8mZVeEA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtVartLfE&amp;md5=52469030077790d14ffd667d03bb0139</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1039/c5cp06184a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lahiri, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Borisenko, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Borodin, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Olschewski, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Endres, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Characterisation of the Solid Electrolyte Interface During Lithiation/Delithiation of Germanium in an Ionic Liquid</span>. <i>Phys.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Study of the Initial Stage of Solid Electrolyte Interphase Formation upon Chemical Reaction of Lithium Metal and N-Methyl-N-Propyl-Pyrrolidinium-Bis(Fluorosulfonyl)Imide</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Budi, Akin; Basile, Andrew; Opletal, George; Hollenkamp, Anthony F.; Best, Adam S.; Rees, Robert J.; Bhatt, Anand I.; O'Mullane, Anthony P.; Russo, Salvy P.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Chem. reaction studies of N-methyl-N-propyl-pyrrolidinium-bis(fluorosulfonyl)imide-based ionic liq. with the Li metal surface were performed using ab initio mol. dynamics (aMD) simulations and XPS.  The mol. dynamics simulations showed rapid and spontaneous decompn. of the ionic liq. anion, with subsequent formation of long-lived species such as LiF.  The simulations also revealed the cation to retain its structure by generally moving away from the Li surface.  The XPS expts. showed evidence of decompn. of the anion, consistent with the aMD simulations and also of cation decompn. and it is envisaged that this is due to the longer time scale for the XPS expt. compared to the time scale of the aMD simulation.  Overall exptl. results confirm the majority of species suggested by the simulation.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Characterization of the Lithium Surface in N-Methyl-N-alkylpyrrolidinium Bis(trifluoromethanesulfonyl)amide Room-Temperature Ionic Liquid Electrolytes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Howlett, P. C.; Brack, N.; Hollenkamp, A. F.; Forsyth, M.; MacFarlane, D. R.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2006</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">153</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) formed on a Li electrode in an N-methyl-N-alkylpyrrolidinium bis(trifluoromethanesulfonyl)amide [p1,x(Tf)2N] room-temp. ionic liq. electrolyte was characterized using XPS, diffuse reflectance FTIR spectroscopy, Raman spectroscopy, and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS).  The SEI is composed mainly of redn. products of the (Tf)2N- anion.  A pronounced difference in compn. was obsd. between the SEI formed on the Li surface and that formed in situ during Li deposition on a Cu substrate.  In the case of the Li surface, native surface species (e.g., Li2O, Li2CO3) persisted in the SEI and dominated the SEI compn.  The surface film formed on Li-deposited-on-Cu did not contain species assocd. with the Li native film.  Instead, in addn. to the anion redn. products, significant quantities of species assocd. with the cation were obsd.  EIS indicated varied Li conduction pathways through the film and that the pathways were in series, suggesting a layered structure.
